center;">8/26\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">10,400\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">3,170\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Asphalt_concrete" title="Asphalt concrete">Asphalt</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align: center;">10/28\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">8,016\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">2,443\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">Concrete</a>\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n</tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black">Statistics (2023)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1237879389"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Total Passengers</th><td class="infobox-data">12,197,553</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source: <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a><sup id="cite_ref-FAA_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />Operations from the FAA<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> GCM<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google Maps<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />passengers from Grupo Aeroportuario del Sureste<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>SJU</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>TJSJ</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>SJU</b>) is a joint civil-military <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> located in suburban <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina, Puerto Rico</a>, three miles (5&#160;km) southeast of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>. It is named for <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn</a>, Puerto Rico\'s first democratically elected governor, and was known as <b>Isla Verde International Airport</b> (<i><b>Aeropuerto Internacional de Isla Verde</b></i>) until it was renamed in February 1985. It is the busiest airport in the Caribbean region by passenger traffic. Over 4 million passengers boarded a plane at the airport per year according to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a>, making it the 48th busiest airport overseen by said federal agency.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport is owned by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Ports_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Ports Authority">Puerto Rico Ports Authority</a> and managed by <a href="/wiki/Aerostar_Airport_Holdings" title="Aerostar Airport Holdings">Aerostar Airport Holdings</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_public%E2%80%93private_partnerships_in_Puerto_Rico" title="List of public\xe2\x80\x93private partnerships in Puerto Rico">public\xe2\x80\x93private partnership</a> which was awarded a lease by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">government of Puerto Rico</a> to operate and manage the airport for 40 years beginning in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> SJU is the second international airport to be <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatized</a> in the United States or its territories, and, as of 2013, is the only currently privatized airport in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Taxis and rental cars can transport travelers to and from the airport. The airport serves as a gateway to the Caribbean islands. SJU covers 1,600 acres (647 ha) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-FAA_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236091366">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}html.client-js body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Special:EditPage/Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2018</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 1945, aware of the importance of aviation for the development of the economy of Puerto Rico, the island government had pointed out the need to build a newer international airport capable of handling the growing air traffic of <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Luis_Ribas_Dominicci_Airport" title="Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport">San Juan International Airport</a>, in Isla Grande, that had been operating since 1929; as well as responding to the needs of the future. Until then Isla Grande had been the main airport of Puerto Rico. As airlines began switching from propeller aircraft to jets, the 4,000 foot (1,200&#160;m) Isla Grande airstrip did not have the necessary distance for modern aircraft to land and take off. (The Isla Grande Airport, now named in honor of Maj. Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci, pilot of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">US Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/F-111_Aardvark" class="mw-redirect" title="F-111 Aardvark">F-111</a>, who was killed in action in <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> in 1986, currently has a runway of 5,542 feet (1,689&#160;m) in length.)\n</p><p>On the other hand, the government had also decided that it should direct the air operations, relying these powers in the Puerto Rico Transportation Authority, created in 1942, which later became the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Ports_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Ports Authority">Ports Authority</a>. The Committee of Airports of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Planning_Board" title="Puerto Rico Planning Board">Planning Board</a> began to study the feasibility of the new airport, submitting in 1944 its plans and studies to the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aeronautics_Board" title="Civil Aeronautics Board">Federal Civil Aeronautics Administration</a>, to determine the most appropriate place.\n</p><p>In 1945, it was determined that the place would be <a href="/wiki/Isla_Verde,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isla Verde, Puerto Rico">Isla Verde</a> (Carolina), to make the airport a metropolitan facility. Construction was approved by the Puerto Rico Planning Board in 1946, and the project began in 1947. During that same year, the Port Authority of Puerto Rico assumed title to and ownership of the Isla Grande Airport and other regional airports, which had been military installations during World War II.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption>Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Marin International Airport in 2009 with clouds overhead</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The design of the new airport was carried out by the firm of <a href="/wiki/Toro-Ferrer" class="mw-redirect" title="Toro-Ferrer">Toro-Ferrer</a>, founded by the architects Miguel Ferrer (1914\xe2\x80\x932004), and architect Osvaldo Toro (1914\xe2\x80\x931995), which were also known for their designs of the <a href="/wiki/Caribe_Hilton_Hotel" title="Caribe Hilton Hotel">Caribe Hilton Hotel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_Building_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Supreme Court Building (Puerto Rico)">Supreme Court</a> of Puerto Rico.\n</p><p>During 1949, the first phase of construction of the Isla Verde Airport was completed: cleaning, filling, leveling and drainage of soils. The second phase also began: paving the runway, taxiways, and platforms.\n</p><p>The certified airlines operating in Puerto Rico in 1950 were <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Lines" title="Eastern Air Lines">Eastern Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caribair_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Caribair (Puerto Rico)">Caribbean Atlantic Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">Iberia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominicana_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n" title="Dominicana de Aviaci\xc3\xb3n">Dominicana Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flying_Tiger_Line" title="Flying Tiger Line">Flying Tigers Airline</a>. The latter contracted the movement of migrant workers to the United States, with the Insular Department of Labor, transferring some 5,706 workers to different points of that nation, at a cost of $55 per passage.\n</p><p>On May 22, 1955, the Puerto Rico International Airport was inaugurated, built on a 1,718.72 acres (695.54&#160;ha) land lot. The facilities, estimated at a cost of $22 million, had a six-story passenger terminal, control tower, 7,800 foot (2,400&#160;m) long runway (8\xe2\x80\x9326), cargo building, fire and police stations, and a hotel.\n</p><p>Hundreds of people, enthusiastic about the new aerial installation, witnessed the inaugural events presided over by <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn</a>. In a part of his eloquent speech, the Governor said: "Impressive is this work in its structure and in its many facilities, but not as impressive as the fact that this center of communications symbolizes the great technical processes that are transforming civilization".\n</p><p>The first year of operations of the new airport produced an upward movement of passengers to 694,199 and a total of 28 million pounds of cargo was handled.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Evolution_of_the_airport">Evolution of the airport</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Evolution of the airport"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>By 1959, major airlines had introduced jets, which significantly reduced flight time and increased flight cruising safety. At the start of operations, the airport had only one runway (8/26), the old control tower on top of the hotel, 3 terminals and a parking lot for 200 cars.\n</p><p>During the beginning of the 60s, several expansion and improvement projects began, starting with the runway extending from 7,800\xe2\x80\x9310,000 feet (2,400\xe2\x80\x933,000&#160;m) in length. Construction of the second runway (10\xe2\x80\x9328) on the south side began in May 1967. The project was completed in 1974 at an approximate cost of $4.2 million. With the introduction of the 747 aircraft, runway 8\xe2\x80\x9326 was reinforced and widened in 1974, and ten years later it was repaved.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_(a_terminal_building)_.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28a_terminal_building%29_.JPG/220px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28a_terminal_building%29_.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28a_terminal_building%29_.JPG/330px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28a_terminal_building%29_.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28a_terminal_building%29_.JPG/440px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28a_terminal_building%29_.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Terminal A facade view from the tarmac</figcaption></figure>\n<p>On January 17, 1983, the two-leveled vehicular access system was built at a cost of approximately $9.2 million. This access separates the arrivals and departures of passengers at different levels, to eliminate traffic congestion.\n</p><p>On February 18, 1985, the Governor of Puerto Rico, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Hern%C3%A1ndez_Col%C3%B3n" title="Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Col\xc3\xb3n">Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Col\xc3\xb3n</a>, converted to law the project to Senate Number 1, officially designating the international airport under the name of Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn, in honor of the first governor of Puerto Rico elected by the people.\n</p><p>The airport served as a hub for Pan Am, <a href="/wiki/Trans_Caribbean_Airways" title="Trans Caribbean Airways">Trans Caribbean Airways</a>, Eastern Air Lines, and for a short period a focus city for <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">TWA</a>. It was also the center for Puerto Rico\'s international airline, <a href="/wiki/Prinair" title="Prinair">Prinair</a>, from 1966 to 1984, when Prinair went bankrupt.\n</p><p>In 1986, <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> together with <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_(airline_brand)" title="American Eagle (airline brand)">American Eagle</a> established a base in Puerto Rico to compete with Eastern Air Lines. At its peak in 2001, the American hub saw over 60 daily mainline flights, mostly to the mainland, and over 100 daily American Eagle flights, mostly to other Caribbean islands on <a href="/wiki/ATR_72" title="ATR 72">ATR 72</a> aircraft.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_(check-in).JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28check-in%29.JPG/220px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28check-in%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28check-in%29.JPG/330px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28check-in%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28check-in%29.JPG/440px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28check-in%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Cape Air check in counters</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_(Gate_A2).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28Gate_A2%29.jpg/220px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28Gate_A2%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28Gate_A2%29.jpg/330px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28Gate_A2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28Gate_A2%29.jpg/440px-Puerto_Rico_%E2%80%94_San_Juan_%E2%80%94_Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport_%28Gate_A2%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Waiting area at Gate A2</figcaption></figure>\n<p>With the expansion of Eastern Airlines and American Airlines facilities, turning Puerto Rico into their Caribbean hub, the historic figure of eight million passengers was reached at the end of 1988. That same year, an investment in expansion and remodeling of $137 million was announced.\n</p><p>The 1990s marked the beginning of important projects to modernize and expand the facilities and services of the airport in response to the boom in passenger and cargo movement and growth projections.\n</p><p>In the period from 1990 to 2000, several infrastructure works were carried out with an investment of approximately $128 million. Some of these include the expansion of the two-level access road to a maximum of 10 lanes on both levels, the new air traffic control tower (designed by <a href="/wiki/Segundo_Cardona" title="Segundo Cardona">Segundo Cardona</a> FAIA of <a href="/wiki/SCF_Architects" title="SCF Architects">SCF Architects</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>), a parallel taxiway connecting lanes 8 and 10, a parking garage, and the first and second phase of the Terminal B expansion, modification, and rehabilitation project.\n</p><p>In subsequent years, from 2000 to 2005, other major projects were initiated and completed such as the third phase of the rehabilitation, modification and expansion of Terminal B and the new B / C connector at a cost of $35.9 million, the construction of a new building for the Air Rescue unit at a cost of $4.1 million, and remodeling the hotel at a cost of $5 million.\n</p><p>Competition from low-cost carriers, together with the financial crisis and oil price shock of 2008, led American to reduce its San Juan operation and consolidate its Caribbean hub flying at <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami</a>. American eventually closed its San Juan base and retired its ATR fleet in 2013 as part of its Chapter 11 restructuring.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> That same year, the airport received major upgrades, including the new Terminal A, new pavement and expansions, new light systems, press conference rooms, consolidated security area for Terminals B, C and D as well as new fast food restaurants along its corridors. In 2012, the new Terminal A was opened, which is currently occupied by <a href="/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The Airport is owned by the Ports Authority but since 2013 it is managed by <a href="/wiki/Aerostar_Airport_Holdings" title="Aerostar Airport Holdings">Aerostar Airport Holdings</a>, in a private public initiative through which a contract was granted to that company to operate the airport for 40 years. This was after observations were made by politicians in and outside of Puerto Rico, and comments were made that privatization was a better solution for the airport. Prior to privatization, management was changed each time a different political party in Puerto Rico took office and this caused disruption, and a lack of a long-term vision for the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-FAA_privatization_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA_privatization-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2024, Frontier Airlines announced the establishment of a crew base in San Juan <sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the past, the airport has been served by <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Condor_(airline)" title="Condor (airline)">Condor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinair" title="Martinair">Martinair</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Europa" title="Air Europa">Air Europa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Cara%C3%AFbes" title="Air Cara\xc3\xafbes">Air Cara\xc3\xafbes</a>, <a href="/wiki/PAWA_Dominicana" title="PAWA Dominicana">PAWA Dominicana</a>, <a href="/wiki/ACES_Colombia" title="ACES Colombia">ACES Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/BWIA_West_Indies_Airways" title="BWIA West Indies Airways">BWIA West Indies Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Antilles" title="Air Antilles">Air Antilles</a>, <a href="/wiki/LIAT" title="LIAT">LIAT</a>, <a href="/wiki/ALM_Antillean_Airlines" title="ALM Antillean Airlines">ALM Antillean Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Jamaica" title="Air Jamaica">Air Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viasa" title="Viasa">Viasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aeropostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Aeropostal">Aeropostal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexicana_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n" title="Mexicana de Aviaci\xc3\xb3n">Mexicana de Aviaci\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volaris" title="Volaris">Volaris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surinam_Airways" title="Surinam Airways">Surinam Airways</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Avianca_Costa_Rica" title="Avianca Costa Rica">LACSA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas" title="Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas">Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominicana_de_Aviacion" class="mw-redirect" title="Dominicana de Aviacion">Dominicana De Aviaci\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wardair" title="Wardair">Wardair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allegiant_Air" title="Allegiant Air">Allegiant Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/ATA_Airlines" title="ATA Airlines">ATA Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(N8)" title="National Airlines (N8)">National Airlines (N8)</a>, <a href="/wiki/AirTran_Airways" title="AirTran Airways">AirTran Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ladeco" title="Ladeco">Ladeco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aeronaves_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Aeronaves de Puerto Rico">Aeronaves de Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coral_Air" title="Coral Air">Coral Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aero_Virgin_Islands" title="Aero Virgin Islands">Aero Virgin Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Operations">Operations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:SJU_San_Juan_Tower.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/SJU_San_Juan_Tower.jpg/220px-SJU_San_Juan_Tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/SJU_San_Juan_Tower.jpg/330px-SJU_San_Juan_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/SJU_San_Juan_Tower.jpg/440px-SJU_San_Juan_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1333" /></a><figcaption>SJU\'s Control Tower designed by <a href="/wiki/Segundo_Cardona" title="Segundo Cardona">Segundo Cardona</a> FAIA (<a href="/wiki/SCF_Architects" title="SCF Architects">SCF Architects</a>)</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_Photo_of_SJU.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Aerial_Photo_of_SJU.jpg/220px-Aerial_Photo_of_SJU.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Aerial_Photo_of_SJU.jpg/330px-Aerial_Photo_of_SJU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Aerial_Photo_of_SJU.jpg/440px-Aerial_Photo_of_SJU.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a><figcaption>An aerial photo of SJU taken on departure</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:PR2_120.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/PR2_120.jpg/220px-PR2_120.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/PR2_120.jpg/330px-PR2_120.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/PR2_120.jpg/440px-PR2_120.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>Teodoro Moscoso Bridge connecting the city of San Juan to the Luis Munoz Marin International Airport in Carolina</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport is Puerto Rico\'s main international gateway and its main connection to the mainland United States. Domestic flights fly between Carolina and other local destinations, including <a href="/wiki/Benjam%C3%ADn_Rivera_Noriega_Airport" title="Benjam\xc3\xadn Rivera Noriega Airport">Culebra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos_Airport" title="Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos Airport">Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Rivera_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Airport" title="Antonio Rivera Rodr\xc3\xadguez Airport">Vieques</a>. The airport is accessed from the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> district of Hato Rey, the island\'s financial district, via the <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Moscoso_Bridge" title="Teodoro Moscoso Bridge">Teodoro Moscoso Bridge</a>. Old San Juan is accessed via the Baldorioty de Castro Expressway (<a href="/wiki/PR-26" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-26">PR-26</a>). \nThe airport serves as the Caribbean <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Sunshine" title="Air Sunshine">Air Sunshine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Airways" title="Silver Airways">Silver Airways</a>, a Focus City for <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> and an operating base for <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">Frontier Airlines</a> (as of June 2024).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> JetBlue is the largest carrier in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, with 51 daily flights on an average day.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Terminals">Terminals</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Terminals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>As of August 2020, Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Airport has one main terminal building with four concourses and a separate terminal with one concourse. However, all terminals are connected. Over the years, the airport has switched between letter designations and number designations. In the late 2010s, the airport incorporated both letter and numbers. The letters are used for the concourses and the numbers used for the airlines\' departure areas in Terminals B, C and D, Terminal A having its own ticketing area.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Terminal_A">Terminal A</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminal A"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In June 2012, Terminal A was opened and occupied solely by <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue Airways</a>, making San Juan a <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">focus city</a>. The terminal originally had seven gates but an additional gate was added for regional airlines during the renovations of Terminals B and C.\n</p><p>As of September 2022, JetBlue uses all gates at Terminal A. Gates A1 and A2 have been used by other airlines in the past such as <a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allegiant_Air" title="Allegiant Air">Allegiant Air</a>. <a href="/wiki/Seaborne_Airlines" title="Seaborne Airlines">Seaborne Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Airways" title="Silver Airways">Silver Airways</a> had temporarily moved their operations to Terminal A from Terminal D as renovations and partial reopening took place. All JetBlue flights, both domestic and international, depart from Terminal A.\n</p><p>As of June 2024, Terminal A is used by <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avelo_Airlines" title="Avelo Airlines">Avelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jetblue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Jetblue Airways">JetBlue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tradewind_Aviation" title="Tradewind Aviation">Tradewind Aviation</a>.\n</p><p>Terminal A also houses The Lounge San Juan,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a VIP <a href="/wiki/Airport_lounge" title="Airport lounge">airport lounge</a> belonging to <a href="/wiki/Priority_Pass" title="Priority Pass">Priority Pass</a> as well as Gates A1 through A8.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Terminal_B_(Concourse)"><span id="Terminal_B_.28Concourse.29"></span>Terminal B (Concourse)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminal B (Concourse)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This $40 million dollar and 365,000 square foot, fully self contained facility opened in 1985 and was designed as a sole terminal for Eastern Airlines accommodating 11 wide body gates.\n</p><p>With Eastern Airlines\xe2\x80\x99 demise, the single carrier 11 gate unit terminal originally designed for Eastern Airlines was altered and expanded in three phases to become a state of the art 25 gate facility servicing over 30 domestic and international airlines and a multitude of concessionaires. The expansion of the existing Terminal B, which resulted in a new concourse, then became to be known as Terminal C. \n</p><p>When Terminal B was closed for renovations, airlines were temporarily moved to Terminals A, C and D. Terminal B reopened after a $130 million renovation in December 2014, with <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Airlines" title="Spirit Airlines">Spirit</a> as its first tenants (with all operations moved in February 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As of September 2022, Terminal B is also used by <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>. All check-in counters for airlines using gates in Terminals B, C and D are all located within the Terminal and Gates B2 through B10 are located within the Concourse.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Terminal_C_(Concourse)"><span id="Terminal_C_.28Concourse.29"></span>Terminal C (Concourse)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminal C (Concourse)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Terminal C was originally built and completed in 1996 as an expansion to Terminal B in an effort to accommodate the growth of American Airlines\xe2\x80\x99 Caribbean Hub. \n</p><p>Terminal C reopened from its $55 million renovation in March 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The letter designation for Terminal C was temporarily discontinued, and the concourse was instead added as an extension to Terminal B.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Terminal B extension was later changed back to Terminal C.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Both Terminals B and C feature high-end retail stores and new restaurants, improved seating as well as automated baggage scanners currently used only by six other airports in the mainland U.S.\n</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a> VIP <a href="/wiki/Airport_lounge" title="Airport lounge">airport lounge</a><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is located at the entrance of Terminal C. This All-Inclusive lounge is operated by Global Lounge Network.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As of June 2024, Terminal C houses gates C2 through C10 and is used by <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">Frontier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">Iberia</a>, international <a href="/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue</a> arrivals as well as local charters.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Terminal_D_(Concourse)"><span id="Terminal_D_.28Concourse.29"></span>Terminal D (Concourse)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminal D (Concourse)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The current Terminal D occupies what were formerly known as Terminals D and E and they were previously occupied solely by <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, its regional affiliate, <a href="/wiki/Executive_Airlines" title="Executive Airlines">Executive Airlines</a>, which operated flights under the <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_(airline_brand)" title="American Eagle (airline brand)">American Eagle</a> brand, and later both <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> and Iberia. American Airlines\' Admirals Lounge continued to operate until March 22, 2014. The former Terminal E area became unused after American Airlines moved their operations to Terminal C in 2015. The American Eagle flights were moved to the previous Terminal D in the late 2000s before being discontinued in April 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal D reopened on March 14, 2023, and is mostly used for small and regional aircraft operators such as <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/InterCaribbean_Airways" title="InterCaribbean Airways">InterCaribbean Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Airways" title="Silver Airways">Silver Airways</a> as well as other carriers. The terminal has five gates set up for regional flights and another three gates set up for high-capacity scheduled and charter flights. These scheduled flights include Delta, Frontier, Spirit and United when Terminals B and C are at maximum capacity. The former eastern end of Terminal D has been walled off, and the former Terminal E remains closed off to the public, both still waiting for renovations. The closed terminal areas and baggage claim area still have old American Airlines branding from their hub operations while the former check-in hall has been renovated for access to the airport hotel and parking.\n</p><p>The new terminal has a more open ambience which will be used as a basis for future renovations at Terminals A, B and C. The cost of renovations is estimated to be at around $14 million.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1248256098">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output destinations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Military"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Air_National_Guard" title="Air National Guard">Air National Guard</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Air_National_Guard" title="Puerto Rico Air National Guard">Puerto Rico Air National Guard</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Mu%C3%B1iz_Air_National_Guard_Base" title="Mu\xc3\xb1iz Air National Guard Base">Mu\xc3\xb1iz ANGB</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/156th_Wing" title="156th Wing">156th Wing</a></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>On March 5, 1969, <a href="/wiki/Prinair_Flight_277" title="Prinair Flight 277">Prinair Flight 277</a>, a <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Heron" title="De Havilland Heron">de Havilland Heron</a> from <a href="/wiki/St._Thomas,_United_States_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Thomas, United States Virgin Islands">St. Thomas, United States Virgin Islands</a>, was attempting to land at the airport when it crashed into mountainous terrain near <a href="/wiki/Luquillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Luquillo, Puerto Rico">Luquillo</a>, killing all 19 on board. An <a href="/wiki/NTSB" class="mw-redirect" title="NTSB">NTSB</a> investigation found that an air traffic controller at the airport mistakenly thought the aircraft was near San Juan when it actually was near <a href="/wiki/Fajardo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Fajardo, Puerto Rico">Fajardo</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On December 31, 1972, baseball star <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente" title="Roberto Clemente">Roberto Clemente</a> and his companions died when their <a href="/wiki/DC-7" class="mw-redirect" title="DC-7">DC-7</a> <a href="/wiki/1972_Puerto_Rico_DC-7_crash" title="1972 Puerto Rico DC-7 crash">crashed</a> soon after <a href="/wiki/Takeoff" title="Takeoff">takeoff</a> from Isla Verde during a relief flight bound for <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>. Neither the bodies of the victims (except for the pilot\'s) nor the plane\'s wreckage was ever found.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On September 26, 1978, an <a href="/wiki/Air_Caribbean_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Air Caribbean (Puerto Rico)">Air Caribbean airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Beech_18" class="mw-redirect" title="Beech 18">Beechcraft D185</a> passenger airplane was landing from <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Hernandez_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rafael Hernandez Airport">Rafael Hernandez Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Aguadilla</a>, after a domestic flight, <a href="/wiki/Air_Caribbean_Flight_309" title="Air Caribbean Flight 309">when it crashed</a> into Barrio Obrero, near <a href="/wiki/Residencial_Las_Casas" title="Residencial Las Casas">Residencial Las Casas</a>, killing all 6 on board. The plane fell on top of a bar, injuring several bar clients, including mechanic Luciano Rivera. Wake turbulence from an Eastern Airlines L-1011 which was also landing was found to be the accident\'s main cause.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On June 27, 1985, an <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/DC-10-10" class="mw-redirect" title="DC-10-10">DC-10-10</a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registered</a> N129AA operating Flight 633 to <a href="/wiki/Dallas/Fort_Worth_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport">Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport</a> with 257 passengers on board aborted take-off from runway 8 after a loud rumbling sound was heard by the crew as the airplane approached <a href="/wiki/V1_speed" class="mw-redirect" title="V1 speed">V1</a>.  Unable to stop the aircraft on the runway, the aircraft ended up nose-first in the lagoon at the end of the runway. A nose gear tire blowout was suspected.  There were no fatalities, and aircraft returned to service six months later.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On July 22, 1986, a <a href="/wiki/Borinquen_Air" title="Borinquen Air">Borinquen Air</a> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_C-53" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas C-53">Douglas C-53</a>D registered N27PR crashed into a lagoon on approach. The aircraft was on a cargo flight to <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Bradshaw_International_Airport" title="Robert L. Bradshaw International Airport">Golden Rock Airport</a>, Saint Kitts and Nevis, when the starboard engine failed shortly after take-off and the crew decided to return to Carolina. One of the two crew members was killed,<sup id="cite_ref-ASN290786_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN290786-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the other was seriously injured.<sup id="cite_ref-MIA86MA217_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIA86MA217-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On March 1, 1989, a Borinquen Air <a href="/wiki/Douglas_C-49" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas C-49">Douglas C-49</a>J registered N28PR ditched on approach following a failure of the port engine.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN010389_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN010389-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although the landing gear was retracted, the crew did not feather the propeller. This resulted in increased drag which made flight impossible. There were no fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-MIA89FA096_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIA89FA096-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The aircraft was on an international cargo flight from <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Bradshaw_International_Airport" title="Robert L. Bradshaw International Airport">Golden Rock Airport</a>, Saint Kitts and Nevis.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN010389_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN010389-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On September 17, 1989, a <a href="/wiki/Tol_Air_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Tol Air Services">Tol Air Services</a> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_C-47" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas C-47">Douglas C-47</a>A registered N100DW was damaged beyond economic repair by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN170989g_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN170989g-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On May 11, 1997, a <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/DC-10-30" class="mw-redirect" title="DC-10-30">DC-10-30</a>, G-NIUK, operated by <a href="/wiki/Flying_Colours_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Flying Colours Airlines">Flying Colours Airlines</a>, Flight 4508 (BA4508), operating as a Title 14 CFR Part 129, scheduled flight to <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>, was evacuated via the slides after the No. 3 (right) engine caught fire at the San Juan International Airport. Visual meteorological conditions prevailed and an IFR flight plan was filed. The airplane was not damaged. The flightcrew of 3, cabin crew of 11, and 248 passengers were not injured. One passenger was seriously injured during the evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On July 9, 1998, an American Airlines <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A300B4" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A300B4">Airbus A300B4</a>-605R registered N80057 operating Flight 574 had a fire in the No. 1 engine shortly after takeoff from Luis Munoz Marin International Airport. The airplane sustained minor damage. The captain, first officer, 7 flight attendants, and 215 passengers were not injured. Twenty-eight passengers reported minor injuries during the post-landing emergency evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On September 24, 1998, a <a href="/wiki/Trans-Florida_Airlines" title="Trans-Florida Airlines">Trans-Florida Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Convair_240" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair 240">Convair 240-13</a> registered N91237 had an engine problem on take-off. It attempted to return to the airport, but lost altitude and was forced to land in a lagoon. Though the aircraft was written off, the two crew and one passenger were uninjured.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On April 4, 2001, a <a href="/wiki/Roblex_Aviation" title="Roblex Aviation">Roblex Aviation</a> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a>A registered N19BA ditched in the ocean after suffering a double engine failure while on a local training flight. Both crew members escaped. The aircraft sustained minor damage.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN040401_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN040401-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-N19BA_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-N19BA-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On May 9, 2004, an <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_(airline_brand)" title="American Eagle (airline brand)">American Eagle</a> <a href="/wiki/ATR_72" title="ATR 72">ATR 72</a> operating Flight 5401 crashed in San Juan, Puerto Rico after the captain lost control of the aircraft while landing. Seventeen people were injured, but there were no fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On March 15, 2012, a Jet One Express cargo <a href="/wiki/Convair_440" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair 440">Convair 440</a> operating a flight to <a href="/wiki/St._Maarten" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Maarten">St. Maarten</a> crashed near the airport, killing its two occupants. The plane went down in a lagoon after the pilot reported engine trouble.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On December 2, 2013, an <a href="/wiki/IBC_Airways" title="IBC Airways">IBC Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Swearingen_SA227-AC_Metro_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Swearingen SA227-AC Metro III">Swearingen SA227-AC Metro III</a> registered N831BC crashed into a terrain near La Alianza, Arecibo, Puerto Rico. The aircraft was on a cargo flight from <a href="/wiki/Las_Am%C3%A9ricas_International_Airport" title="Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas International Airport">Santo Domingo</a>, Dominican Republic, when the crew lost control of the aircraft for reasons that could not be determined. Both crew members were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On August 9, 2014, a <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> operating flight 704 to <a href="/wiki/JFK_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="JFK International Airport">JFK International Airport</a>, New York had to abort takeoff after one of the engines caught fire. All 186 passengers were evacuated from the aircraft. Two women were slightly hurt during evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On June 3, 2017, a fatal crash happened at nearby Pinones Beach when an Air America Airlines airplane, on its way from San Juan to Culebra, tried to perform an emergency landing at the airport, going into the beach\'s waters instead. A 15-year-old female died, while a 14-year-old female, a 45-year-old male passenger and the aircraft\'s male pilot were rescued injured but alive.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>On September 22, 2021, a passenger onboard <a href="/wiki/Jetblue" class="mw-redirect" title="Jetblue">Jetblue</a> Flight 261 arriving from Boston attempted to enter the cockpit after choking a crew member with his own tie. The passenger tried to make a call but failed, proceeded to run towards the front galley, demanding in Spanish to be shot before attempting to enter the cockpit when the First Officer opened the door. The passenger was restrained.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: In popular culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>Various scenes of the 1976 <a href="/wiki/La_Pandilla" title="La Pandilla">La Pandilla</a> teen comedy musical, "<a href="/wiki/La_Pandilla_en_Apuros" title="La Pandilla en Apuros">La Pandilla en Apuros</a>", were filmed at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The airport is featured in <a href="/wiki/Hunter_S._Thompson" title="Hunter S. Thompson">Hunter S. Thompson</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rum_Diary_(novel)" title="The Rum Diary (novel)">The Rum Diary</a>.</i></li>\n<li>In the 1984 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Conexi%C3%B3n_Caribe" title="Conexi\xc3\xb3n Caribe">Conexi\xc3\xb3n Caribe</a></i>, juvenile music group <a href="/wiki/Los_Chicos" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Chicos">Los Chicos</a> arrived at the Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport and boarded an <a href="/wiki/Oceanair" title="Oceanair">Oceanair</a> airplane.</li>\n<li>Music group <a href="/wiki/Menudo_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Menudo (band)">Menudo</a> recorded the music video for their song "Claridad", in 1981 at the nearby Isla Verde Beach in Pi\xc3\xb1ones. An Eastern Airlines Lockheed <a href="/wiki/L-1011" class="mw-redirect" title="L-1011">L-1011</a> aircraft landing at Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport can be seen in the background.</li>\n<li>The airport is seen in several scenes of the 2007 action film <a href="/wiki/Illegal_Tender_(film)" title="Illegal Tender (film)"><i>Illegal Tender</i></a>, where a Puerto Rican youngster flies to the Island from the mainland United States several times.</li>\n<li>In 2021, the airport was renovated in preparation to host the <a href="/wiki/Miss_World_2021" title="Miss World 2021">2021 Miss World</a> Pageant which was held in San Juan on March 17, 2022.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span
